<userid>105085964196592368702</userid><username>Grant Willis<//username><Date>1509251148917<//Date>< rate>

< review>
I went in with no appointment, at 3:30pm and on a Friday. it was a half  full waiting room. so I thought I was gonna be there till 6pm. HOWEVER, the security guards pointed me to the touch screen, self check in, and were shouting the names or numbers being called out to ensure people where hearing them called ( which sounds annoying, but I get how frustrating it would be to miss your call). Generally it was Very helpful especially since there was a rush or calls at the end. I personally didn't have time to finish filling out my Social security card Replacement Form, because I had been called up so quickly. I was helped by a MR. Wood, who was done with my paperwork and was incredibly helpful and even asked questions about if it was for employment (which it was, and I had forgotten to ask if it would work for an employment opportunity) so he provided it with a stamp to verify the date to assist me further. I was so impressed by the quick and thoroughly comprehensive service by Mr. wood and the friendly assistance from the security guards. I Would not mind having to go back to this office if needed. I don't intend to unless necessary but it definitely would not be a dreaded trip. Say in comparison to the Pain of the DMV, or to the bureaucracy and mind numbing boredom of the Emergency room ( yes I listed the places to their descriptions correctly).
So thank you again Mr. Wood, and the security guards that worked 10-27-2017, and Social Security Office for being a government service that finally gets How to be efficient.

if you have a bad visit, maybe you should double check what you need to bring FIRST or be over prepared to answer possible questions designed to keep people from screwing you over, and help keep the service from having to go slow and extract your info that you should have ready and on hand.

By the way I walked in at 3:30 and left exactly at 4pm. when I left the waiting room was near empty. So props. to all staff that day, sorry I don't know your names.</review>

So as of today i no longer can say i really enjoy this restaurant which saddens me. The original people who ran this business no longer work there, they are gone. So, to be fair, this is one of those instances where you don't do better until you know better (or in this case-tasted better). I thought the price was outstanding for the sandwich I received. However, I found that every time I would order the bread was so hard it would scrape the top of my mouth. They would say okay sure, but I noticed a hesitation. When I got home there would be no extra and what's worse, I don't think they were using fresh ingredients because the "jalape√±os" were sweet not spicy. Brake pads are recommended at 3mm and anything under 1mm is specified as "at metal". Brake pads do not have rivets like brake shoes and if the pads get past 1mm the caliper is at risk of the piston coming out too far and ceasing. The brake rotors had a lip and there was not enough material to be machined. Although the rotor was clean and smooth it would be below the discard spec. The manufacturer recommends to replace the brake pads and rotors for BMW , Mercedes, Fiat, Mini Cooper and Audi for all brake replacements with no recommendations for resurfacing. When performing all other  brake jobs the brake rotors need to be either machined or replaced, a "pad slap" is highly discouraged due to brake noise and possible failure due to the rotors being too thin. The manufacturer has rotor discard specifications to ensure safety. If a rotor has a lip at the edge the rotor is below its machine spec and needs  be replaced.
